PARKING GENERALLY
§ 77.001 PROHIBITION AGAINST PARKING ONS STREETS OR HIGHWAYS.
   (A)   Upon any street or highway outside of a business or residence district
no person shall stop, park or leave standing any vehicle, whether attended or
unattended, upon the paved or main-traveled part of the street or highway, but
in every event an unobstructed width of the street or highway opposite a
standing vehicle shall be left for the free passage of other vehicles and a
clear view of such stopped vehicles shall be available from a distance of 200
feet in each direction upon such highway or street.
   (B)   This section shall not apply to the driver of any vehicle which is
disabled while on paved or main-traveled portion of a street or highway in suck
a manner and to such extent that it is impossible to avoid stopping and
temporarily leaving such disabled vehicle in such position.
(W.Va Code § 17C-13-1) (Res. passed 6-3-2019) Penalty, see §
77.999
§ 77.002 POLICE MAY REMOVE ILLEGALLY STOPPED VEHICLES.
   (A)   Whenever any police office finds a vehicle standing upon a street or
highway in violation of §
77.001, such officer is hereby authorized to move such vehicle or require the
driver or other person in charge of the vehicle to move the same, to a position
off the paved or main-traveled part of such street or highway.
   (B)   Whenever any police officer finds a vehicle unattended upon any bridge
or crossway or in any tunnel where such vehicle constitutes an obstruction to
traffic, such officer is hereby authorized to provide for the removal of such
vehicle to the nearest garage or other place of safety.
(W.Va Code § 17-C-13-2) (Res. passed 6-3-2019) Penalty, see §
77.999
§ 77.003 PROHIBITED STOPPING, STANDING OR PARKING PLACES.
   (A)   No person shall stop, stand or park a vehicle except when necessary to
avoid conflict with other traffic or in compliance with law or the directions
of a police officer or traffic control device, in any of the following places:
      (1)   On a sidewalk;
      (2)   In front of a public or private driveway;
      (3)   Within an intersection;
      (4)   Within 15 feet of fire hydrant;
      (5)   On a crosswalk;
      (6)   Within 20 feet of a crosswalk at an intersection;
      (7)   Within 30 feet upon the approach to any flashing beacon, stop sign
or traffic control signal located at the side of a roadway;
      (8)   Between a safety zone and the adjacent curb or within 30 feet of
points on the curb immediately opposite the ends of a safety zone, unless a
different length os indicated by signs or markings;
      (9)   Within 50 feet of the nearest rail of a railroad crossing;
      (10)   Within 20 feet of the driveway entrance to any fire station and on
the side of a street opposite the entrance to any fire station within 75 feet
such entrance (when proper signs posted);
      (11)   Alongside or opposite any street excavation or obstruction when
stopping, standing or parking would obstruct traffic;
      (12)   On the roadway side of any vehicle stopped or parked at the edge
or curb of a street;
      (13)   Upon any bridge or other elevated structure upon a street or
highway or within a street or highway tunnel;
      (14)   At anyplace where signs prohibit stopping, standing or parking, or
where the curbing of street is painted yellow or red, or at any place in excess
of the maximum time limited by signs;
      (15)   Within 20 feet of any mail receptacle served regularly by a
carrier using a motor vehicle for daily deliveries, if such parking interferes
with or causes delay in the carrier’s schedule;
      (16)   Upon any controlled-access highway;
      (17)   At any place on any street or highway where the safety and
convenience of the traveling public is thereby endangered; and
      (18)   Over or across any lines or marks established by the municipality
to indicate parking spaces.
   (B)   No person shall move a vehicle not lawfully under his or her control
into any such prohibited area or away from the curb such distance is unlawful.
(W.Va Code § 17C-13-3) (Res. passed 6-3-2019) Penalty, see §
77.999
§ 77.004 VEHICLES PARKED ON PRIVATE PROPERTY.
   No drivers of a vehicle shall stop, park or leave standing unattended any
vehicle on a private road or driveway or on private property without having
express or implied permission from the owner, tenant or lessee of such land.
The owner, tenant or lessee of such private road or driveway or private
property may more, or have moved, any vehicle stopped, parked or left standing
unattended on his or her private road, driveway or private property as above
prohibited without any liability for the cost of moving any vehicle, nor shall
he or she be liable to the owner of the vehicle for any damage done to such
vehicle in moving it, unless the owner, tenant or lessee of such private road
or driveway or private property was negligent in removing or authorizing the
removal of the vehicle. The owner of such vehicle shall be responsible to the
person removing such vehicle for paying all removal costs. Any person who
removes any vehicle under the provisions of this section shall notify the State
Department of Public Safety of such action, and, in addition notify the Police
Department.
(W.Va Code § 17C-14-13) (Res. passed 6-3-2019) Penalty, see §
77.999
§ 77.005 MANNER OF ANGLE AND PARALLEL PARKING.
   (A)   Every vehicle stopped or parked upon a roadway where there is an
adjacent curb shall be stopped or parked with the curb-side wheels of such
vehicle parallel with and not more than 18 inches from the curb, unless it is
impossible to approach so close to the curb; in such case the stop shall be as
close to the curb as possible and only for the time necessary to discharge and
receive passengers or to lad or unload merchandise.
   (B)   This section does not apply to streets or parts thereof where angle
parking is lawfully permitted. However, no angle parking shall be permitted on
a state or federal-aid route unless approved by the State Commissioner of
Highways.
   (C)   Upon streets where angle parking is permitted, no person shall stop,
stand or park a vehicle other than at the angle to the curb or edge of the
roadway as is indicated by appropriate signs or marks.
   (D)   No vehicle shall be stopped or parked on a road or street with the
vehicle facing in a direction other than the direction of travel on that side
of the road or street.
(Res. passed 6-3-2019) Penalty, see §
77.999
§ 77.006 HANDICAPPED PARKING.
   (A)   For the purpose of this section, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
      PHYSICALLY DISABLED PERSON. Any person who has sustained a temporary
disability rendering it unduly difficulty and burdensome for him or her to
walk.
      PHYSICALLY HANDICAPPED PERSON WITH LIMITED MOBILITY. Any person who
suffers from permanent physical condition making it unduly difficulty and
burdensome for such person to walk.
   (B)   (1)   Free stopping, standing or parking placed marked “reserved for
disabled persons” shall be designated on close proximity to all state, county
and municipal buildings and other public facilities. Such places shall be
reserved solely for physically disabled and handicapped persons during the
hours that such buildings are open for business.
      (2)   Any person whose vehicle properly displays a valid special
registration plate, mobile windshield place card or decal, may park the vehicle
for unlimited periods of time in parking zones unrestricted as to length of
parking time permitted; provided, that this privilege does not mean that the
vehicle may park in any zone where stopping, standing or parking is prohibited
or which creates parking zones for special types of vehicle or which prohibits
parking during heavy traffic periods during specified rush hours or where
parking would clearly present a traffic hazard. To extent any provision of any
ordinance of the municipality is contrary to the provisions of the section, the
provisions of the section shall take precedence and shall apply.
      (3)   The privileges provided for in this division (B) shall apply only
during those times when the vehicle is being used for the transportation of a
physically handicapped or disabled person. No person shall knowingly exercise,
or attempt to exercise, such privileges at a time when the vehicle is not being
used for the transportation of a physically handicapped or disabled person.
   (C)   No person shall stop, stand or park a motor vehicle in an area
designated, zoned or marked for the handicapped or physically disabled, when
such person is not physically disabled or handicapped and does not have
displayed upon his or her vehicle a distinguishing insignia for the handicapped
issued by the Commissioner of Highways; provided, that any person in the act of
transporting a handicapped or physically disabled person, as defined by this
section, may stop, stand or park a motor vehicle not displaying a
distinguishing insignia for the handicapped or physically disabled, for the
limited purposes of providing, however, that such vehicle shall be promptly
moved after the completion of such limited purposes.
(W.Va Code § 17C-13-6) (Res. passed 6-3-2019) Penalty, see §
77.999
§ 77.007 ABANDONED AND JUNK VEHICLES.
   (A)   Definitions. For the purpose of this section, the following
definitions shall apply unless the context clearly indicates or requires a
different meaning.
      ABANDONED MOTOR VEHICLE. Any motor vehicle, or major part thereof, which
is inoperative and which has been abandoned on public or private property for
any period of time over five days, other than in an enclosed building or in a
licensed salvage yard or at the business establishment of a demolisher, or any
motor vehicle, or major part thereof, which has remained illegally on public or
private property for any period of time over five days, or any motor vehicle,
or major part thereof, which is unattended, discarded, deserted and unlicensed
and is not in an enclosed building, a licensed salvage yard or the actual
possession of a demolisher.
      JUNKED MOTOR VEHICLE. A motor vehicle or any part thereof, other than an
on-premises farm utility vehicle, which:
         (a)   Is discarded, wrecked, ruined, scrapped or dismantled;
         (b)   Cannot pass the state inspection required by W. Va. Code §§ 17C-
16-1 et seq.; and
         (c)   Is either not serving a functional purpose or use or is not in
an enclosed building, a licensed salvage yard or the actual possession of a
demolisher.
      MOTOR VEHICLE. A vehicle which is or was self-propelled, including, but
not limited to, automobiles, truck, buses and motorcycles.
(W.Va Code § 17-24-2)
   (B)   Abandoning or depositing prohibited.
      (1)   No person shall abandon a motor vehicle upon the right-of-way of
any public street or highway, upon any other public property, or upon any
private property which he or she does not own, lease, rent or otherwise control
unless it is at a licensed salvage yard or at the business establishment of a
demolisher.
(W.Va Code § 17-24-3)
      (2)   No person shall place or deposit any junked motor vehicle upon the
right-of-way of any public street or highway or upon any other public property;
nor shall any person place or deposit any junked motor vehicle upon any private
property which he or she does not own, lease, rent or otherwise control unless
it be at a licensed salvage yard or at the business establishment of a
demolisher.
(W.Va Code § 17-24-4)
(Res. passed 6-3-2019) Penalty, see §
77.999
§ 77.008 PARKING FOR CERTAIN PURPOSES PROHIBITED.
   No person shall park any vehicle upon any street within the municipality for
the principal purpose of:
   (A)   Displaying such vehicle for sale;
   (B)   Displaying advertising;
   (C)   Washing, greasing or repairing such vehicle, except repairs made
necessary by an emergency; or
   (D)   Relieving the crowded condition of any parking lot, used car lot,
automobile sales lot, repair garage, automobile sales agency or used car sales
agency.
(Res. passed 6-3-2019) Penalty, see §
77.999
§ 77.009 TRUCK LOADING ZONES.
   No person shall stop stand or park a vehicle for any purpose for any length
of time other than for the expeditious unloading and delivering or pickup and
unloading materials in any place marked as a truck loading zone during hours
when the provisions applicable to such zones are in effect. In no case shall
the stop for loading and unlading of materials exceed 30 minutes.
(Res. passed 6-3-2019) Penalty, see §
77.999
§ 77.010 BUS STOPS AND TAXI CAB STANDS.
   (A)   No person shall stop, stand or park a vehicle other than a bus in a
bus stop, or other than a taxi cab in a taxicab stand when any such stop or
stand has been officially designated and appropriately posted, except that the
driver of a passenger vehicle may temporarily stop therein for the purpose of
and while actually engaged in loading or unloading passengers when such
stopping does not interfere with any bus or taxicab waiting to enter or about
to enter such zone, and then only for a period not to exceed three minutes, if
such stopping is not prohibited therein by posed signs.
   (B)   The operator of a bus shall not stop, stand or park such vehicle upon
any street at any place for the purpose of loading or unloading passengers or
their baggage other than at a bus stop so designated and posted as such, except
in case of an emergency.
   (C)   The operator of a bus shall enter a bus stop on a public street in
such manner that the bus when stopped to load or unload passengers or baggage
shall be in a position with the right front wheel of such vehicle not further
than 18 inches from the curb and the bus approximately parallel to the curb so
as not to unduly impede the movement of other vehicular traffic.
   (D)   The operator of a taxicab shall not stand or park such vehicle upon
any street at any place other than in a taxi cab so designated and posted as
such. This provision shall not prevent the operator of a taxicab from
temporarily stopping in accordance with other stopping or parking provisions at
any loading place for the purpose of and while actually engaged in the
expeditious loading or unloading of passengers.
(Res. passed 6-3-2019) Penalty, see §
77.999
§ 77.011 PARKING IN ALLEYS AND NARROW STREETS; EXCEPTIONS.
   (A)   No person shall stop, stand or park any vehicle upon a street, other
than an alley, in such a manner or under such conditions as to leave available
less than ten feet of width of roadway for free movement of vehicular traffic,
except that a driver may stop temporarily during the actual loading or
unloading of passengers or when directed to by a police officer or traffic
control signal.
   (B)   Except as otherwise provided by law, no person shall stop, stand or
park a vehicle within an alley except while actually loading and unloading,
then only for a person not to exceed 30 minutes.
(Res. passed 6-3-2019) Penalty, see §
77.999
§ 77.012 REGISTERED OWNER PRIMA FACIE LIABLE FOR UNLAWFUL PARKING.
   In any hearing on a charge of illegally parking a motor vehicle, testimony
that a vehicle bearing a certain license place was found unlawfully parked as
prohibited by the provisions of the traffic code and further testimony that the
records of the Department of Motor Vehicles shows that the license place was
issued to the defendant, shall be prima facie evidence that the vehicle which
was unlawfully parked was so parked by the defendant. A certified copy of
registration from the Department of Motor Vehicles shall be proof of such
ownership.
(Res. passed 6-3-2019)
PARKING SPACES
§ 77.025 AREAS ESTABLISHED.
   In areas which it shall indicated upon the Traffic Control Map, Council may
cause parking spaces to be marked by lines on the curb or pavement or by other
appropriate markings, or on the sidewalks adjacent to each such parking space
may cause to be erected a sign indicating that parking can be made by vehicle
in this space for a period not to exceed two hours; and there shall be no fee
charged for parking therein. However, this vehicle parked within this parking
space must not remain for a period of more than two hours; and in the event
this term is exceeded the owner of such vehicle or operator of such vehicle
becomes subject to the provisions in §
77.999.
(Res. passed 6-3-2019) Penalty, see §
77.999
§ 77.026 HOURS OF OPERATION; HOLIDAYS.
   These parking regulations set out above as to parking only in spaces for a
period not to exceed two hours shall not operate on Sundays and the following
holidays, namely: New Year’s Day, Memorial Day, Independence Day, Labor Day,
Thanksgiving Day, and Christmas Day.
(Res. passed 6-3-2019)
§ 77.027 OVERTIME PARKING.
   If any vehicle remains parked in any parking space for a length of time in
excess of two hours, and a police officer notes that the parking time in this
parking space has expired, such vehicle in such parking space for a period of
over two hours shall be considered a violation of this subchapter.
(Res. passed 6-3-2019) Penalty, see §
77.999
§ 77.028 VIOLATIONS.
   No owner of operator of any motor vehicle or other vehicle shall permit his
or her vehicle to be parked in a parking space for a period of time in excess
of time allocated to that parking space by the rules and regulations
promulgated by Council and described at each particular parking space.
(Res. passed 6-3-2019) Penalty, see §
77.999
§ 77.029 RESTRICTED PARKING AREAS.
   Council may also cause certain spaces to be marked indicated on the Traffic
Control Map as non-parking areas, loading and unloading areas or restricted
parking areas limited to five minute parking, 30 minute parking, one hour
parking or other time limit parking. These parking areas shall be marked by
paint or shall have such limitations indicated on a sign erected at such area.
Council may further change these regulations from time to time as needed in
order to facilitate traffic parking, loading and unloading and the like.
(Res. passed 6-3-2019)
GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 77.040 BUSINESS DISTRICT DEFINED.
   The Council has designated the following streets and avenues as the business
district within the town and has designated said district for free parking:
Eighth (Main) Street from the bridge to Fifth Avenue; Ninth Street from First
Avenue to Fifth Avenue; First Avenue from Eighth Street to Ninth Street; Second
Avenue and Third Avenue from Seventh Street to Ninth Street; Fourth Avenue from
the North end of the Marlinton Depot to Ninth Street; and Tenth Avenue from
Judge Street to Jury Street.
(Ord. passed 5-7-2012)
§ 77.041 AREA ONE.
   (A)   The following place shall be designated as “Area One” and shall be
used only for permit parking: on Third Avenue along the Southern States’ fence.
   (B)   Each permit shall cost the sum set by Council from time to time per
month and shall be purchased at intervals covering at least six months each
time.
(Ord. passed 5-7-2012)
§ 77.042 AREA TWO.
   (A)   The following place shall be designated as “Area Two” and shall be
used only for permit parking: the vacant lot between the Flower Garden and the
Pocahontas Times.
   (B)   Each permit shall cost the sum set by Council from time to time per
month and shall be purchased at intervals covering at least six months each
time.
(Ord. passed 5-7-2012)
§ 77.043 PARKING PROHIBITED.
   The Council finds that it is necessary to limit the free parking of vehicles
on Eighth (Main) Street to a reasonable amount of time, during the normal 6:00
a.m. to 8:00 p.m. business hours. The Council further finds that it is
necessary to restrict business owners, business employees and residents who
live on Eighth (Main) Street to no parking during these normal business hours
on Eighth Street. The Council also finds that the purpose of free parking on
Eighth (Main) Street is to encourage and facilitate business in the town.
(Ord. passed 5-7-2012)
U.S. ROUTE 219 PARKING
§ 77.055 TITLE.
   This subchapter shall be known as the “U.S. Route 219 Parking Ordinance”.
(Ord. passed 1-4-1992)
§ 77.056 OBSTRUCTION.
   The Council is concerned about the flow of traffic in the newly annexed
portion of the town reaching from the southern end of Burns Motor Freight to
the southern end of the also newly annexed Community of Riverside. There are
numerous businesses in this area on the eastern side of U.S. Route 219 which
requires much of the traffic which utilizes these businesses to cross a lane of
traffic entering these businesses and exiting these businesses. The amount of
traffic which uses these businesses is sufficiently great that the potential
exists for problems in this area. The Council specifically finds that vehicles
parking near Route 219 obstructs the view of drivers entering and exiting these
businesses and that it is imperative for a regulation to be passed to minimize
the possibility of accidents in this area due to vision being obscured by
parked vehicles.
(Ord. passed 1-4-1992)
§ 77.057 REGULATION.
   From and after the effective date of this subchapter it shall be illegal for
any person to park a vehicle along U.S. Route 219 from the southern edge of the
fence of Burns Motor Freight as it adjoins the right- of-way of U.S. Route 219
northward to the southern end of the Community of Riverside so that any part of
the vehicle is within eight feet of the paved portion of the roadway. The
southernmost point of the Community of Riverside shall be determined by
extending a line along the fence which divides the real estate currently owned
by Tom Burns and the Community of Riverside to the edge of the right-of-way of
U.S. Route 219.
(Ord. passed 1-4-1992) Penalty, see §
77.999
RIGHTS-OF-WAY
§ 77.070 TITLE.
   This subchapter shall be known as the “Right-of-Way Obstruction Ordinance”.
(Ord. passed 3-5-1984)
§ 77.071 OBSTRUCTION.
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for any person or persons to obstruct the free
passage of traffic on any public right-of-way within the town. The term RIGHT-
OF-WAY shall include, but shall not be limited to, streets, avenues, alleyways,
but includes all passageways used by the public or by public conveyances such
as vehicles owned by the town and used on property owned by the town.
   (B)   It shall be sufficient to support a conviction under this section if
the accused shall:
      (1)   Block a right-of-way with a vehicle or other obstruction to prevent
the free flow of traffic through the right-of-way;
      (2)   Block a lane of traffic on a street or avenue so that it would be
necessary for another vehicle to cross the centerline of the street or avenue
or leave the paved portion of the street or avenue or to drive in an area
customarily reserved for parked vehicles in order to pass the obstruction; or
      (3)   Block the free flow of traffic to and from property owned by the
town.
(Ord. passed 3-5-1984) Penalty, see §
77.999
§ 77.072 REGULATION APPLIED EQUALLY; DEFENSES.
   This subchapter applies equally to situations involving an intentional
obstruction and to situations in which traffic is blocked by persons allowing
their vehicles to remain in the right-of-way. It shall not be a defense to
assert that the accused or another person remained in the vehicle during the
period of obstruction, nor shall it be a defense for the accused to assert that
the engine in the vehicle was still running.
(Ord. passed 3-5-1984)
§ 77.073 EXEMPTIONS.
   Specifically exempted from this subchapter are the following:
   (A)   The breaking down of a vehicle in the public right-of-way, provided
that the owner or driver of the vehicle remains with the vehicle; and
   (B)   Delivery vehicles making actual deliveries to businesses, provided
that such delivery vehicles do not park on State Route 39 and do not obstruct
the public right-of-way for more than one-half hour.
(Ord. passed 3-5-1984)
TRUCK PARKING
§ 77.085 TITLE.
   This subchapter shall be known as the “Marlinton Truck Regulation
Ordinance”.
(Ord. passed 2-3-1986)
§ 77.086 REGULATION.
   The Town Council finds that it is in the best interests of the people of the
town to regulate the movement and parking of trucks within the town limits.
This action is necessitated by the noise created by the unnecessary or
excessive use of such vehicles at night and by the added stress such vehicles
place on certain streets within the town. Streets other than Route 39 are not
constructed to withstand heavy traffic or heavy vehicles and the underlying
natural foundation is not conducive to road building.
(Ord. passed 2-3-1986)
§ 77.087 ILLEGAL PARKING.
   (A)   From and after the effective date of this subchapter, it shall be
unlawful to park trucks of greater than two-ton capacity on public property in
residential areas within the town.
   (B)   It shall be unlawful for drivers of trucks of over two-ton capacity to
drive upon or park upon any public roadway or public property within the town
except for Route 39 and further except for local deliveries.
   (C)   It shall be unlawful to park any truck of a capacity of two tons or
over on any public property within the town.
(Ord. passed 2-3-1986) Penalty, see §
77.999
§ 77.088 RIGHTS.
   Nothing herein shall limit the rights of individuals or businesses to park
their trucks on their own property, to drive to their homes or places of
business from Route 39 or to drive to Route 39 from their homes or places of
business while engaged in the actual pursuit of business. Nothing herein shall
limit the rights of the town or other public county, state or federal agency to
operate trucks in the town.
(Ord. passed 2-3-1986)
HOSPITAL ZONE
§ 77.100 PARKING IN QUIET ZONE.
   (A)   Statement of policy. The Town Council finds that there are problems
now existing on Main Street (Eighth Street) which need correction. Within the
Hospital Zone, extending from the eastern most corner of the Bank of Marlinton
to the Greenbrier River, there are congregations of people in the evening hours
and these people make loud and unnecessary noise, thereby disturbing the
patients in the Pocahontas Memorial Hospital. The Council further finds that as
a further complication of this matter that people will impede the flow of
traffic through the town by standing in the street and talk to others in cars
or on the sidewalk. These people in the street endanger themselves and increase
the likelihood of automobile accidents. The Town Council finds that they have
not just the right, but the responsibility to do what is necessary to correct
these problems in order to maintain proper quiet in the Hospital Zone and to
maintain the safety of people congregating lawfully within the town.
   (B)   From and after the effective date of this section, it shall be
unlawful for anyone to park his or her vehicle within the Hospital Zone in the
town between the hours of 10:00 p.m. and 6:00 a.m. Exceptions to this general
rule are those people parking in order to attend services at the Marlinton
Presbyterian Church, those people going to the Hospital, or those people
parking in order to participate in some legitimate business activity with any
business located in the Hospital Zone. However, it shall remain unlawful for
these people parking lawfully to create any type of disturbance while they are
so lawfully parked in the Hospital Zone. The police authority shall have the
right to inform any such offending person of his or her violation and inform
him or her of what is necessary to correct that violation. Thereafter, any
person continuing to violate this section shall be subject to the penalty
provisions in §
77.999 and shall be further subject to having his or her vehicle towed from the
Hospital Zone at the offender’s expense. If the town places small signs on the
parking meters, then it shall not be incumbent upon the police authority to
inform the violator first before taking any action under this section. If the
police authority informs any person of his or her violation of this section
once, then the officer shall have no further requirement under this section to
inform the violator on subsequent occasions concerning subsequent violations.
(Ord. passed 8-14-1987) Penalty, see §
77.999
§ 77.999 PENALTY.
   (A)   See §
70.99 for general traffic code penalty.
   (B)   (1)   The fines for the following traffic violations shall be as set
by Council from time to time.
      (2)   The Police Department is directed to prepare and have produced an
envelope type violation ticket setting forth on the face thereof, the fines
listed out in the division (B)(1) above, and the Police Department is
authorized to purchase such numbers of such envelope-type tickets or summonses
may be necessary in the proper administration of the Department.
   (C)   Whoever violates §§
77.025 through
77.029 shall be fined an amount set by Council from time to time for each
offense.
   (D)   Vehicles in violation of §§
77.040 through
77.043 can be towed at the owner’s expense. A violation of §§
77.040 through
77.043 can be punishable by a fine set by Council from time to time plus court
cost, per each citation.
   (E)   The penalty for a violation of §§
77.055 through
77.057 shall be either incarceration in the county jail for a period not to
exceed 30 days or a fine set by Council from time to time or both such fine and
imprisonment.
   (F)   The penalty for a violation of §§
77.070 through
77.073 shall be a fine set by Council from time to time.
   (G)   The penalty for a violation of any of §
77.087 above shall be a fine set by Council from time to time.
   (H)   For any violation under §
77.100, any person found guilty or pleading guilty shall be subject to a fine
set by Council from time to time, plus mandatory costs. For second and
subsequent violations, there shall be a fine set by Council from time to time.
(Ord. passed 3-5-1984; Ord. passed 2-3-1986; Ord. passed 8-14-1987; Ord. passed
1-4-1992; Ord. passed 5-7-2012; Res. passed 6-3-2019)
