IN GENERAL
§ 150.001 TITLE.
   This Town of Marlinton building chapter is enacted pursuant to the authority
granted to the town under W. Va. Code § 8-12-16.
(Prior Code, § 4-101) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017)
§ 150.002 ADOPTION OF STATE BUILDING CODE.
   (A)   The town on February 6, 2012 adopted the State Building Code, as
amended as the town’s building code. This chapter has been adopted to
supplement and localize the State Building Code, as amended and adopted in the
2022 State Building Code. Nothing contained in this chapter is intended to
abrogate any provision of the 2022 State Building Code and should any provision
of this chapter be found in conflict with this chapter, the 2022 State Building
Code shall control. The 2022 State Building Code is made a part of this chapter
as if set out herein verbatim.
   (B)   A copy of the 2022 State Building Code shall be available for public
inspection in the office of the Mayor of the town during normal business hours.
(Prior Code, § 4-102) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017; Ord. passed 7-25-2022)
TECHNICAL CODES
§ 150.015 DEFINITIONS.
   (A)   Specific. For the purpose of this chapter, the following definition
shall apply unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different
meaning.
      TECHNICAL CODE. As used in this chapter, shall mean any building code,
plumbing code, electrical code or any other code adopted by ordinance to be
applicable within the town.
   (B)   Other definitions. For the purpose of this chapter, the following
definitions shall apply unless the context clearly indicates or requires a
different meaning.
      BUILDING OFFICIAL. The building inspector or his or her authorized
representative.
      CHIEF ADMINISTRATOR. The Mayor of the Town of Marlinton, West Virginia.
      CHIEF APPOINTING AUTHORITY. The Mayor, with the approval of the Town
Council when such approval is required.
      ELECTRICAL INSPECTOR. The building inspector or other authorized
representative.
      LEGAL DEPARTMENT. The Town Attorney.
      LOCAL GOVERNING BODY. The Mayor and Town Council.
      MUNICIPALITY. The Town of Marlinton.
      PLUMBING INSPECTION DEPARTMENT. The office of the building inspector or
authorized representative.
      PLUMBING OFFICIAL. The building inspector or authorized representative.
(Prior Code, § 4-201) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017)
§ 150.016 ADOPTION.
   (A)   There is hereby adopted by reference for the purpose of establishing
rules and regulations, the 2022 State Building Code as promulgated by the West
Virginia State Fire Commission, and the provisions thereof shall be controlling
within the corporate limits of the town. A copy of such will be available in
the town offices and available for public inspection during regular business
hours.
   (B)   The standards and requirements set out by the International Code
Council and American Standards Institute, as listed below, shall have the same
force and effect as if set out verbatim herein (except that any and all
references to the ICC Electrical Code shall mean the National Electrical Code).
   (C)   There is hereby adopted the following codes:
      (1)   The International Building Code, Edition, 2015;
      (2)   The International Plumbing Code, Edition, 2015;
      (3)   The International Mechanical Code, Edition, 2015;
      (4)   The International Property Maintenance Code, Edition, 2015;
      (5)   The International Residential Code, Edition, 2015;
      (6)   The ICC/ANSI Standards for Accessibility and Usable Buildings and
Facilities, Edition, 2009;
      (7)   The International Existing Building Code, Edition, 2015; and
      (8)   The National Electrical Code, Edition, 2014.
(Prior Code, § 4-202) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017; Ord. passed 7-25-2022)
§ 150.017 CONFLICTS.
   (A)   Whenever there arises a conflict between the State Fire Code and the
State Building Code, the State Fire Code shall take precedence.
   (B)   Whenever there arises a conflict between the International Plumbing
Code portion of the State Building Code and the rules of the West Virginia
Department of Health and Human Resources, the rules of the West Virginia
Department of Health and Human Resources shall take precedence.
   (C)   Whenever there arises a conflict between the State Building Code and
the West Virginia Code, the West Virginia Code shall take precedence.
   (D)   In the event that any portion of the State Building Code conflicts
with any provision of the National Electrical Code, and such provision relates
to electrical work, the applicable provisions of the National Electrical Code
shall take precedence.
(Prior Code, § 4-203) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017)
BUILDING AND STRUCTURES
§ 150.030 VIOLATIONS; INJUNCTIVE RELIEF UPON VIOLATION.
   (A)   Violations. It shall be a violation of this chapter of the town for
any person, firm or corporation to erect, construct, alter, extend, remove,
demolish, maintain, fail to maintain, provide, fail to provide, occupy, let to
another to occupy or permit another person to occupy any premises, property,
structure or equipment regulated by the town, or cause same to be done contrary
to or in conflict with or in violation of any of the provisions of the
ordinances of the town and any of the technical codes adopted by the town, or
fail to obey a lawful order of the building inspector, or to remove or deface a
placard or notice posted or issued by the building inspector.
   (B)   Injunction. In the case of any revisions, the Mayor or such person as
the Mayor may designate is hereby authorized and empowered to institute and
maintain a suit to restrain by injunction the violation of the ordinances of
the town or any technical code notwithstanding the penalty for the violation
thereof.
(Prior Code, § 4-301) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017)
§ 150.031 ADOPTED; PURPOSE.
   There is hereby adopted by the town, for the purpose of providing additional
safety to life and property from fire and other hazards incident to the
construction, alteration, repair, removal, demolition, use and occupancy of
buildings, structures or premises, that certain code known as the town’s
Building Code.
(Prior Code, § 4-302) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017)
§ 150.032 SCOPE.
   These regulations shall control all matters concerning the construction,
alteration, addition, repair, removal, demolition, use, location, occupancy and
maintenance of all buildings and structures in the town; except as such matters
are otherwise provided for in other ordinances or statutes.
(Prior Code, § 4-303) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017)
§ 150.033 CODE REMEDIAL.
   This code shall be construed to secure its expressed intent, which is to
ensure public safety, health and welfare insofar as they are affected by
building construction through structural strength, adequate egress facilities,
sanitary equipment, light and ventilation, and in general, to secure safety to
life and property from all hazards incident to the design, erection, repair,
removal, demolition or use and occupancy of buildings, structures or premises.
(Prior Code, § 4-304) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017)
§ 150.034 MATTERS NOT PROVIDED FOR.
   Any requirement essential for structural, fire or sanitary safety of an
existing or proposed building or structure, or essential for the safety of the
occupants thereof, and which is not specifically covered by any ordinances of
the town or any technical code, shall be determined by the building inspector.
(Prior Code, § 4-305) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017)
§ 150.035 CONTINUATION OF UNLAWFUL USE.
   The continuation of occupancy or use of a building or structure, or any part
thereof, contrary to the ordinances of the town or any technical code, shall be
deemed a violation and subject to the penalties prescribed hereunder and each
day such conditions is allowed to continue and shall constitute a separate
violation of this code.
(Prior Code, § 4-306) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017)
§ 150.036 ORDINARY REPAIRS; GENERAL.
   Ordinary repairs to structures may be made without application or notice to
the building inspector; but such repairs shall not include the cutting away of
any wall, partition or portion thereof, the removal or cutting of any
structural beam or bearing support, or the removal or change of any required
means of egress, or rearrangement of parts of a structure affecting the exitway
requirements; nor shall ordinary repairs include addition to, alteration of,
replacement or relocation of any stand pipe, water supply, sewer, drainage,
drain leader, gas, soil, waste, vent or similar piping, electrical wiring or
mechanical or other work affecting public health or general safety.
(Prior Code, § 4-307) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017)
§ 150.037 INSTALLATION OF SERVICE EQUIPMENT.
   When the installation, extension, alteration or repair of an elevator,
moving stairway, mechanical equipment, refrigeration, air conditioning or
ventilating apparatus, plumbing, gas piping, electric wiring, heating system or
any other equipment, it shall be unlawful to use such equipment until a
certificate of approval has been issued therefor by the building inspector.
(Prior Code, § 4-308) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017) Penalty, see §
150.999
§ 150.038 MAINTENANCE.
   (A)   All buildings and structures and all parts thereof, both existing and
new, shall be maintained in a safe and sanitary condition.
   (B)   All service equipment, means of egress, devices and safety guards
which are required in a building or structure, shall be maintained in good
working order.
(Prior Code, § 4-309) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017)
§ 150.039 OWNER RESPONSIBILITY.
   The owner of any building or structure shall be responsible for the safe and
sanitary maintenance of the building or structure and its exitways at all
times.
(Prior Code, § 4-310) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017)
§ 150.040 CONTINUATION OF EXISTING USE.
   The legal use and occupancy of any structure existing as of the date of
adoption of this chapter or for which it had been heretofore approved, may be
continued without change, except as may be specifically deemed necessary by the
building inspector for the general safety and welfare of the occupants and the
public.
(Prior Code, § 4-311) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017)
§ 150.041 CHANGE IN USE.
   It shall be unlawful to make any changes in the use or occupancy of any
building or structure without approval of the building inspector, and
certification that such a structure meets the provisions of the ordinances of
the town governing building construction for the proposed new use and
occupancy, and that such change does not result in any hazard to public safety
or welfare.
(Prior Code, § 4-312) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017) Penalty, see §
150.999
EXISTING STRUCTURES
§ 150.055 APPLICATION.
   Except as otherwise provided herein, existing structures, when altered or
repaired as herein specified, shall be made to conform to the full requirements
for new buildings or structures.
(Prior Code, § 4-313) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017)
THE BUILDING INSPECTOR
§ 150.070 OFFICE OF BUILDING INSPECTOR; ESTABLISHED; APPOINTMENT AND GENERAL
POWERS AND DUTIES OF BUILDING INSPECTOR; DELEGATION OF AUTHORITY.
   (A)   The office of building inspector is hereby established, which shall be
headed by the building inspector and shall have such other personnel as may
from time to time be authorized by the Town Council.
   (B)   The building inspector shall be appointed or designated by the Mayor,
with the advice and consent of the Town Council, and shall have the powers and
perform the duties prescribed for the office by this title and all other
ordinances, resolutions or orders of the Town Council, and as prescribed by the
West Virginia Code for municipal officers charged with the administration and
enforcement of building, plumbing, gas, electrical and other technical codes
which municipalities are authorized to adopt pursuant to state law.
   (C)   The building inspector may delegate powers to and require performance
of duties by such deputies, assistants and other personnel as may from time to
time be assigned or detailed by the Mayor and Town Council.
   (D)   For all purposes under all technical codes adopted by the Town of
Marlinton and all other ordinances of the Town of Marlinton, the building
inspector shall be the responsible “building official”, “code official” or such
other designation for such officer as used within such, technical codes or
ordinances of the town. The building inspector shall be vested with all
authority, duty and responsibility permitted and authorized by all technical
codes and other ordinances of the town and to the full extent of the licenses
and certificates possessed by the building inspector.
(Prior Code, § 4-401) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017)
§ 150.071 SPECIFIC POWERS AND DUTIES.
   (A)   The building inspector or authorized representative shall receive all
applications required to be submitted to the town. The building inspector shall
make or cause to be made all inspections required to be made; and issue all
permits and certificates required to be issued by the town by this code and by
all technical codes adopted by the town. The building inspector shall examine
premises for which permits have been issued and make necessary inspections to
see that the provisions of law and ordinances of the town are complied with and
that construction and other work is safely prosecuted. The building inspector
shall enforce all provisions of all technical codes adopted by the town. The
building inspector shall, when requested by proper authority, or when the
public interest so requires, make investigations in connection with matters
referred to in the provisions of the town and the technical codes and render
written reports thereon. To enforce compliance with law and ordinances of the
town, to remove illegal or unsafe conditions, to secure the necessary
safeguards during construction, or to require adequate exit facilities in
building and structures, he or she shall issue such notices or orders as may be
necessary to accomplish the purposes of this title and all other ordinances of
the town and technical codes adopted by the town.
   (B)   Inspections required under the provisions of this code and all
technical codes adopted by the town shall be made by the building inspector or
duly authorized agents. The building inspector may accept reports of inspectors
of recognized inspection services, after investigation of their qualifications
and reliability. No certificate called for by any provision of any ordinance or
technical codes shall be issued on such reports unless they are in writing and
certified by a responsible officer of such service.
   (C)   The building inspector shall keep comprehensive records of
applications, or permits issued, of certificates issued, of inspections made,
of reports rendered, and of notices or orders issued. The building inspector
shall retain on file copies of required plans and all documents relating to
construction work so long as any part of the building or structure to which
they relate may be in existence.
   (D)   All such records shall be open to public inspection during normal
business hours, but shall not be removed from the office of the building
inspector, however the building inspector shall have photo copies available to
any citizen who may request same.
   (E)   The building inspector shall make written reports to the Mayor once
each month, or more often if requested, including statements of permits and
certificates, and orders issued.
   (F)   The building inspector shall create and prescribe forms of all
notices, orders, inspections, reports and any other document necessary to
perform the duties hereunder in the enforcement of the ordinances of the town,
building codes and all technical codes. Such forms shall be open to public
inspection during normal business hours.
   (G)   When in the discharge of the building inspector’s duties, the building
inspector exercising professional judgement determines that any violation(s) or
deviation(s) of this code or any technical code should not result in a formal
notice or order, the building inspector may exercise professional discretion
and is authorized to issue a warning. Any warning so issued shall describe the
violation(s) or deviation(s) and shall specify a time within which such
violation(s) or deviation(s) shall be remedied, such time period not to exceed
ten calendar days and further notify the owner or responsible person that
failure to comply therewith will result in the issuance of a notice or order
and a fine.
(Prior Code, § 4-402) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017)
§ 150.072 DUTY OF OTHER OFFICERS TO COOPERATE.
   The building inspector may request and shall receive, so far as may be
necessary in the discharge of his or her duties, the assistance and cooperation
of other town officers and employees.
(Prior Code, § 4-403) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017)
§ 150.073 OFFICIAL RECORDS.
   An official record shall be kept of all business and activities of the
building inspector specified in ordinances of the town and all technical codes
adopted by the town, and all such records shall be open to public inspection
during regular business hours.
(Prior Code, § 4-404) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017)
§ 150.074 ADDITIONAL DUTIES AND POWERS OF BUILDING INSPECTOR; GENERAL.
   The building inspector shall enforce all the provisions of the ordinances of
the town and all technical codes and shall act on any question relative to the
mode or manner of construction and the materials to be used in the erection,
addition to, alteration, repair, removal, demolition, installation of service
equipment, and the location, use, occupancy and maintenance of all buildings
and structures.
(Prior Code, § 4-405) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017)
§ 150.075 APPLICATION AND PERMITS.
   The building inspector shall receive applications and issue permits for all
construction and alteration of buildings and structures and inspect the
premises for which such permits have been issued and enforce compliance with
the ordinances of the town and all technical codes adopted by the town.
(Prior Code, § 4-406) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017)
§ 150.076 BUILDING NOTICES AND ORDERS.
   The Building inspector shall issue all necessary notices or orders to remove
illegal or unsafe conditions, to require the necessary safeguards during
construction, to require adequate exit ways in existing buildings and
structures, and to ensure compliance with all ordinances of the town and all
technical codes adopted by the town for the safety, health and general welfare
of the public.
(Prior Code, § 4-407) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017)
§ 150.077 INSPECTIONS.
   The building inspector shall make all the required inspections, or may
accept reports of inspection by authoritative and recognized services or
individuals; and all reports of such authoritative service or individuals; or
the building inspector may engage such expert as may be deemed necessary to
investigate and report upon unusual technical issues that may arise, subject to
approval of the Mayor and any additional costs incurred by the town for such
unusual technical issue shall be paid by the applicant.
(Prior Code, § 4-408) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017)
§ 150.078 DEPARTMENT RECORDS.
   The building inspector shall keep official records of applications received,
permits and certificates issued, fees collected, reports of inspections,
warnings notices and orders issued. Such records shall be retained in the
official records as long as the building or structure to which they relate
remains in existence unless otherwise provided by ordinances.
(Prior Code, § 4-409) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017)
§ 150.079 APPROVED MATERIALS AND EQUIPMENT.
   All materials, equipment and devices approved for use by the building
inspector shall be constructed and installed in accordance with such approval.
(Prior Code, § 4-410) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017)
§ 150.080 PRELIMINARY INSPECTION.
   Before issuing a permit, the building inspector may examine or cause to be
examined all buildings, structures and sites for which an application has been
filed for a permit to construct, enlarge, alter, repair, remove, demolish or
change the use thereof.
(Prior Code, § 4-411) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017)
§ 150.081 REQUIRED INSPECTIONS.
   After issuing a building permit the building inspector shall conduct such
inspections from time to time during construction and upon completion of the
work for which a permit was issued; and shall maintain a record of all such
examinations and inspections and of any and all violations.
(Prior Code, § 4-412) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017)
§ 150.082 FINAL INSPECTION.
   Upon completion of the building or structure, and before issuance of a
certificate of use and occupancy a final inspection shall be made, any
violation of the approved plans and permit shall be noted and the holder of the
permit shall be notified of the discrepancies and given an appropriate period
of time to remedy and comply with the permit issued, not to exceed 30 days.
(Prior Code, § 4-413) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017)
§ 150.083 RIGHT OF ENTRY.
   In the discharge of these duties, the building inspector or authorized
representative shall have the authority to enter at any reasonable hour any
buildings, structures or premises in the town.
(Prior Code, § 4-414) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017)
§ 150.084 WHEN PERMIT IS REQUIRED.
   It shall be unlawful to construct, enlarge, alter or demolish a structure;
or change the occupancy of a building or structure, exitway or sanitary
provisions; or to change to another use; or to install or alter any equipment
for which provision is made or the installation of which is regulated by
ordinances of the town and all technical codes adopted by the town, without
first filing an application with the building inspector in writing and
obtaining the required permit therefor; except that ordinary repairs, shall be
exempt from the need for a permit. Such permit must be issued prior to the
commencement of any work upon the building or structure. Failure to comply with
this section shall subject the owner a fine as set forth in this code.
(Prior Code, § 4-415) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017) Penalty, see §
150.999
§ 150.085 FORM OF APPLICATION.
   The application for a permit shall be submitted in such form as the building
inspector may prescribe and shall be accompanied by the required fee.
(Prior Code, § 4-416) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017)
§ 150.086 BY WHOM APPLICATION IS MADE.
   Application for a permit shall be made by the owner of the building or
structure, or the owner’s agent, or by the licensed engineer or architect
employed in connection with the proposed work. If the application is made by a
person other than the owner, it shall be accompanied by a duly verified
affidavit of the owner or the qualified person making the application that the
proposed work is authorized by the owner and that the applicant is authorized
to make such application. The full names and addresses of the owner, applicant
and of the responsible officer, if the owner or lessee is a corporation, shall
be stated in the application.
(Prior Code, § 4-417) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017)
§ 150.087 DESCRIPTION OF WORK.
   The application shall contain a general description of the proposed work,
its location, the use and occupancy of all parts of the building or structure
and of all portions of the site or lot not covered by the building or
structure, and such additional information as may be required by the building
inspector. Two sets of plans for the construction shall be submitted with the
application.
(Prior Code, § 4-418) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017)
§ 150.088 AMENDMENTS TO APPLICATION.
   Amendments to any application or other record accompanying the same may be
filed at any time before the completion of the work for which the permit is
sought or issued; and such amendments shall be deemed part of the original
application and shall be filed therewith. Notwithstanding the foregoing, the
building inspector shall act promptly on any and all such amendments and render
a decision in writing, within ten calendar days of the filing thereof.
(Prior Code, § 4-419) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017)
§ 150.089 ACTION ON APPLICATION.
   The building inspector shall examine or cause to be examined all
applications for permits and amendments thereto within a reasonable time after
filing not to exceed five calendar days. If the application or the plans do not
conform to the requirements of all technical codes adopted by the town and
ordinances of the town such application shall be rejected in writing, stating
the reasons therefor. If satisfied that the proposed work conforms to the
requirements of all codes and ordinances applicable thereto, the building
inspector shall issue a permit therefor as soon as practicable, not to exceed
ten calendar days from the date of filing.
(Prior Code, § 4-420) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017)
§ 150.090 SUSPENSION OF PERMIT.
   Any permit issued shall become invalid if the authorized work is not
commenced within six months after issuance of the permit, or if the authorized
work is suspended or abandoned for a period of six months after the
commencement of work.
(Prior Code, § 4-421) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017)
§ 150.091 SIGNATURE TO PERMIT.
   The building inspector shall sign every permit, order or notice issued under
all technical codes and ordinances of the town; or may authorize a subordinate
to affix such a signature thereto.
(Prior Code, § 4-422) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017)
§ 150.092 APPROVED PLANS.
   The building inspector shall stamp or endorse in writing both sets of plans
“APPROVED” and one set of such approved plans shall be retained by the building
inspector and the other set shall be kept at the construction site, open to
inspection of the building inspector or authorized representative at all times.
(Prior Code, § 4-423) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017)
§ 150.093 REVOCATION OF PERMITS.
   The building inspector may revoke a permit or approval issued in the case of
any false statement or misrepresentation of fact in the application or plans on
which the permit or approval was based.
(Prior Code, § 4-424) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017)
§ 150.094 POSTING OF PERMIT.
   A true copy of the building permit shall be posted in a conspicuous location
on the construction site for public inspection during the entire time of
prosecution of the work and until removed by the building inspector.
(Prior Code, § 4-425) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017)
§ 150.095 PAYMENT OF FEES.
   A permit shall not be issued until all fees have been paid.
(Prior Code, § 4-426) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017)
§ 150.096 COMPLIANCE WITH PERMIT.
   The permit shall be a license to proceed with the work and shall not be
construed as authority to violate, cancel or set aside any of the provisions of
this code, any technical code adopted by the town or other ordinance, except as
specifically stipulated by modification or legally granted variation as
described in the application and permit.
(Prior Code, § 4-427) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017)
§ 150.097 COMPLIANCE WITH PERMIT.
   All work shall conform to the approved application and plans for which the
permit has been issued and any approved amendments thereto. Any deviation
therefore shall subject the owner to a fine as set forth in this code.
(Prior Code, § 4-428) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017)
§ 150.098 DEMOLITION OF STRUCTURES; SERVICE CONNECTIONS.
   Before a structure can be demolished or removed, the owner or agent shall
notify all utilities having service connections within the structure such as
water, electric, gas, sewer and any other connection. A permit to demolish or
remove a structure shall not be issued until the owner shall obtain a written
statement from all utilities, that their respective service connections and
appurtenant equipment, such as meters and regulators, have been removed or
sealed and plugged.
(Prior Code, § 4-429) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017)
§ 150.099 NOTICE TO ADJOINING OWNERS.
   Only when written notice has been given by the applicant to all owners of
all adjoining lots of the applicants intent to demolish a structure such that
adjoining lot owners may experience a temporary interruption of utility
services necessitated by the proposed work, shall a permit be granted for the
removal of a building or structure. Proof of compliance herewith shall be by
certified mail receipt or sworn affidavit or other proof acceptable to the
building inspector.
(Prior Code, § 4-430) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017)
§ 150.100 LOT REGULATION.
   Whenever a structure is demolished or removed, the premises shall be
maintained free from all unsafe or hazardous conditions.
(Prior Code, § 4-431) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017)
§ 150.101 MOVED STRUCTURES.
   Buildings and structures moved into or within the town shall comply with all
of the provisions of, all technical codes adopted by the town and ordinances
relating to new buildings and structures.
(Prior Code, § 4-432) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017)
§ 150.102 FEES.
   The payment of the fee for the construction, alteration, removal or
demolition and for work done in connection with or concurrently with the work
contemplated by a building permit, shall not relieve the applicant or holder of
the permit from the payment of any other fees that may be prescribed by law or
ordinance for water taps, sewer connections, electrical permits, fees for signs
and display structures, or other appurtenant structures, or fees for
inspections, certifications of use and occupancy or other privileges or
requirements.
(Prior Code, § 4-433) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017)
§ 150.103 NEW CONSTRUCTION, MOBILE HOMES AND PREFABRICATED HOMES AND
ALTERATIONS.
   The fee for a building permit shall be $25 base fee plus $5 per $1,000 of
value (or any portion thereof).
(Prior Code, § 4-434) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017)
§ 150.104 MOVING OF BUILDINGS.
   The fee for a building permit for the moving of a building or structure into
the town or from one lot to another within the town or to a new location on the
same lot shall be $25.
(Prior Code, § 4-435) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017)
§ 150.105 DEMOLITION.
   The fee for a permit for the demolition of a building or structure shall be
$25.
(Prior Code, § 4-436) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017)
§ 150.106 SIGNS.
   The fee for signs, billboards and other display structures for which permits
are required shall be paid consistent with the provisions of the town’s sign
regulations.
(Prior Code, § 4-437) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017)
RENTAL UNIT MAINTENANCE
§ 150.120 CERTIFICATE OF USE AND OCCUPANCY.
   A building or structure intended to be used for rental housing shall not be
used nor occupied in whole or in part until a certificate of use and occupancy
has been issued by the building inspector.
(Prior Code, § 4-501) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017)
§ 150.121 PURPOSE.
   The purpose of this subchapter shall be is to promote health and safety
standards for rental housing and to secure and preserve the integrity and
character of residential districts within the town. These standards relate to
the condition, maintenance and occupancy of rental dwelling units and are
intended to ensure that rental housing is safe, sanitary and suitable in
accordance with applicable provisions of the State Building Code, the
International Property Maintenance code, and all codes and other ordinances
adopted by the town.
(Prior Code, § 4-502) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017)
§ 150.122 SCOPE.
   This subchapter applies to all rental dwelling units within the town. This
subchapter shall not apply to owner occupied dwellings wherein roomers or
boarders are maintained in common living areas nor to hotels, motels,
dormitories, bed and breakfast establishments or other transient residential
units.
(Prior Code, § 4-503) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017)
§ 150.123 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   CERTIFICATE OF USE AND OCCUPANCY. The certificate issued by the building
inspector which permits the use of a building and which certifies compliance
with the provisions of law for the use and occupancy of the building in its
several parts together with any special stipulations or conditions.
   CODE OFFICIAL. The building inspector charged with the administration and
enforcement of the ordinances and technical codes adopted by the Town of
Marlinton, or a duly authorized agent.
   DWELLING UNIT. A single unit providing complete, independent living
facilities for one or more persons, including permanent provisions for living,
sleeping, eating, cooking and sanitation.
   OWNER OCCUPIED. Occupied by the actual property owner or by any person or
persons related thereto by blood, marriage or adoption and where no rent is
paid.
   RENTAL DWELLING UNIT. Any dwelling unit, which is offered in whole or part
for residential purposes and for which rent is paid.
(Prior Code, § 4-504) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017)
§ 150.124 ILLEGAL CONDITIONS.
   An owner or operator shall not rent or offer for rent any dwelling unit for
use in whole or in part for human habitation unless a written application for a
certificate of use and occupancy has been filed for such dwelling unit and a
valid certificate of use and occupancy has been issued for such dwelling unit
by the building inspector certifying that an inspection found the premises to
be in compliance with this and all applicable ordinance of the town, the State
Building Code, the International Property Maintenance Code, and all technical
codes adopted by the town.
(Prior Code, § 4-505) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017)
§ 150.125 APPLICATION FOR CERTIFICATE OF USE AND OCCUPANCY.
   (A)   Generally. The building inspector is hereby authorized and directed to
create and maintain such applications, forms, guidelines, inspection sheets,
notices, orders and such other documents needful and necessary to perform the
duties under all applicable ordinances of the town.
   (B)   Initial application. Application for a certificate of use and
occupancy for a rental dwelling unit where none has previously been issued
shall be filed prior to occupancy of any rental dwelling unit.
   (C)   Renewal application. An application for renewal of an existing
certificate of use and occupancy shall be filed at least 30 calendar days
before the expiration date of an existing certificate of use and occupancy.
   (D)   Initial applications. Initial applications upon passage of ordinance
an applications for a certificate of use and occupancy for any and all rental
dwelling units in existence upon passage of this chapter shall be filed within
90 calendar days from the date of passage of this and all related ordinances.
The building inspector shall cause to be published a Class II legal
advertisement in the Pocahontas Times stating the date of passage and the
deadline for filing.
(Prior Code, § 4-506) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017)
§ 150.126 FEES AND CONDITIONS.
   The Town Council shall establish a fee schedule for inspections,
cancellations, re-inspections and application fees. The same shall be provided
for the building inspector and are to be posted in the office of the building
inspector. No permit shall be issued before any and all fees have been paid.
(Prior Code, § 4-507) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017)
§ 150.127 INSPECTION PROCEDURE.
   (A)   Once a properly executed application is filed and all fees paid
therefore, the building inspector shall conduct a full and complete inspection
of the subject unit within ten calendar days of filing. The owner or the
owner’s agent shall accompany the building inspector and provide access to any
and all areas of the building or structure for inspection.
   (B)   If, after inspection, any dwelling unit found to conform to all
requirements therefore, the building inspector shall issue a certificate of use
and occupancy within ten calendar days. Such certificate shall be valid for two
calendar years from the date of issue, unless sooner revoked.
   (C)   A certificate of use and occupancy issued for any unit shall be
transferrable upon sale of such unit. Such certificate must be posted within
the dwelling unit in a conspicuous location.
(Prior Code, § 4-508) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017)
§ 150.128 VIOLATIONS.
   (A)   Upon inspection, the discovery of any violations and/or deviations of
any applicable technical code, State Building Code or any ordinance of the
town, that do not involve habitability nor safety, the building inspector shall
issue a notice of violation which shall provide the owner a specific period of
time no to exceed 30 calendar days to correct the same; however, such shall not
constitute grounds to refuse nor withhold, a certificate of use and occupancy
for such unit. However, in any proceeding to enforce this chapter, any
technical code adopted by the town, or the building code of the town and any
notice of violation where the owner has failed or refused to correct same and
comply such violations may be used to remove any certificate of use or
occupancy issued for any unit.
   (B)   Upon inspection, the discovery of violations and/or deviations of any
applicable technical code adopted by the town, State Building Code or any
ordinance of the town, such that habitability is or may be affected but such do
not pose an imminent hazard, the building inspector shall issue a notice of
violation which shall require the owner a specific period of time, not to
exceed 30 calendar days, to correct all such violations and/or deviations and
the building inspector shall issue a conditional certificate of use and
occupancy to the owner. In the event that the owner fails or refuses to correct
all violations and/or deviations within the specified time period, such
conditional certificate of use and occupancy shall be immediately revoked and
the building inspector shall issue an order to vacate. From and after the
revocation of the conditional certificate of use and occupancy and the order to
vacate continued human habitation of the rental unit shall be prohibited. Each
day thereafter wherein human habitation occurs shall constitute a separate
violation.
   (C)   The building inspector may upon written request of the owner of any
rental unit, extend the period of compliance with any notice of violation
issued by the building inspector where in the professional opinion of the
building inspector good cause exists for the delay in compliance and there
exists no immediate threat to the health or safety of any occupants of the
rental unit or the building or structure but shall not exceed an additional 30
calendar days. In such case, the building inspector shall issue a conditional
certificate of use and occupancy and an amended notice of violation providing
the future time period to correct any violation and/or deficiency the building
inspector deems appropriate.
   (D)   Upon inspection, the discovery of any violation and/or deviation from
any applicable technical code adopted by the town, State Building Code or any
ordinance of the town which in the professional opinion of the building
inspector constitutes good cause to withhold or revoke any certificate of use
and occupancy the building inspector shall immediately issue an order to
vacate. Further, upon inspection, the discovery of any violations and/or
deviations which in the professional opinion of the building inspector pose an
immediate threat to the health or safety of the occupants of a rental unit or
the building or structure, the building inspector shall issue an order of
immediate vacation of the rental unit or the building or the structure, as the
case may require. Any occupancy in violation of the order to vacate shall
subject the owner and/or occupants to the penalties provided under this chapter
and each day such occurs shall constitute a separate violation of this chapter.
(Prior Code, § 4-509) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017)
§ 150.129 NOTICES AND ORDERS.
   (A)   Notice of violation. Whenever in the professional opinion of the
building inspector a notice of violation should be issued, the same shall be in
writing, on a form promulgated by the building inspector and shall include, at
a minimum, the following:
      (1)   The application number to which the notice relates;
      (2)   The owner’s name as shown on the application;
      (3)   The description of the rental dwelling unit as shown on the
application;
      (4)   A clear statement of the reasons for the issuance of the notice;
      (5)   The code violation found;
      (6)   The remedial action necessary for compliance;
      (7)   A specific time period and date for compliance;
      (8)   Statement of the owner’s right of appeal; and
      (9)   Such notice shall be signed and dated by the building inspector.
   (B)   Service of notice. Any notice of violation issued under the authority
of the building inspector shall be personally delivered to the owner or posted
on the front door of the rental unit to which it applies, such delivery or
posting shall have the same effect as personal service and notice upon the
owner.
   (C)   Order of revocation or order of denial of a certificate of use and
occupancy. Whenever in the professional opinion of the building inspector an
order of revocation of a certificate of use and occupancy should be issued or
an order of denial of a certificate of use and occupancy should be issued, the
same shall be in writing, on a form promulgated by the building inspector and
shall include all of the information required to be included in a notice of
violation and shall also contain a clear and concise statement setting forth
all reasons and bases for the issuance of the order.
   (D)   Order to vacate. Whenever in the professional opinion of the building
inspector an order to vacate should be issued, the same shall be in writing, on
a form promulgated by the building inspector and shall include all the
information required to be included in a notice of violation and shall also
contain a clear and concise statement setting forth all reasons and bases for
the issuance of the order and the specific facts and violations found by the
building inspector which in the professional opinion of the building inspector
pose an immediate threat to the health and safety of the occupants of the
rental unit or the building or structure.
   (E)   Conditional certificate of use and occupancy. Whenever in the
professional opinion of the building inspector violations and/or deviations of
any applicable technical code adopted by the town, State Building Code or any
ordinance of the town exist in a rental unit and/or building or structure but
such violations and/or deviations do not pose an immediate threat to the health
and safety of the occupants thereof such that the building inspector issues a
conditional certificate of use and occupancy such conditional certificate shall
state upon its face that such certificate is “Conditional” and shall state the
violations and/or deviations found; and shall state the date of expiration
thereof. In the event such violations and/or deviations are not remedied prior
to the expiration date thereof, upon expiration thereof, the building inspector
shall issue an order to vacate and the owner of such rental unit shall cause
the unite and/or building or structure to be immediately vacated and shall be
required to commence the application process anew as if no certificate of use
and occupancy had ever been issued.
(Prior Code, § 4-510) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017)
§ 150.130 APPEALS.
   (A)   Any owner of any rental unit or building or structure shall have an
absolute right of appeal from any decision, notice or order of the building
inspector.
   (B)   Such appeal shall be to the town’s Building Maintenance Board as
created by the town ordinances and such appeal shall be in writing and set out
therein all information regarding the rental unit, building or structure; all
information regarding the inspection and challenged decision of the building
inspector; and the basis for such appeal. The building inspector shall provide
a form for such appeal.
   (C)   Any appeal must be filed in the office of the Mayor within 20 calendar
days of the action by the building inspector appealed.
   (D)   In all cases the Building Maintenance Board shall convene upon said
appeal within 30 calendar days of the filing of any appeal unless the owner
requests an expedited appeal and sets forth good cause for an expedited appeal
in which case the Building Maintenance Board shall convene within 15 calendar
days after the filing of such appeal.
   (E)   The owner shall be given notice by regular United States mail as to
the date and time of the convening of the Building Maintenance Board and such
owner shall attend in person and may have legal counsel to present the owner’s
appeal. The owner may call witnesses and present testimony and evidence, under
oath.
   (F)   The Town Attorney shall represent the town at such hearing and shall
present evidence and testimony on behalf of the town.
   (G)   Upon conclusion of the proceedings the Building Maintenance Board
shall deliberate and return a decision upon the appeal. Such decision of the
Building Maintenance Board shall be final unless either party, the owner or the
town, shall obtain an order from the circuit court of the county reversing the
decision of the Building Maintenance Board.
   (H)   The filing of an appeal shall not stay any order or notice of the
building inspector but such appeal shall stay the enforcement of any monetary
penalties assessed, until the final decision of the Building Maintenance Board
is rendered.
   (I)   Any decision of the Building Maintenance Board shall be in writing and
a copy thereof served by regular United States mail upon the owner or upon
counsel for the owner.
(Prior Code, § 4-511) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017)
CONSTRUCTION AND ALTERATION
§ 150.145 BUILDINGS HEREAFTER ALTERED.
   A building or structure hereafter enlarged, extended or altered to change
from one use to a different use, in whole or in part, or a building or
structure hereafter altered for which a certificate of use and occupancy has
not been heretofore issued, shall not be occupied or used until a certificate
shall have been issued by the building inspector, certifying that the work has
been completed in accordance with the provisions of all applicable codes and
ordinances of the town relates to the proposed use of the building or
structure.
(Prior Code, § 4-601) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017)
§ 150.146 EXISTING BUILDINGS.
   Upon written request from the owner of an existing building or structure,
the building inspector shall issue a certificate of use and occupancy, provided
that there are no violations of any technical code adopted by the town or
ordinance of the town, and it is established, after inspection and
investigation, that the proposed use of the building or structure can be
established.
(Prior Code, § 4-602) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017)
§ 150.147 CONTENTS OF CERTIFICATE.
   When a building or structure is entitled thereto, the building inspector
shall issue a certificate of use and occupancy within ten calendar days after
submission of the written application. The certificate shall certify compliance
with the provisions of all technical codes adopted by the town and all other
applicable ordinances of the town for the purpose for which the building or
structure may be used in its several parts.
(Prior Code, § 4-603) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017)
§ 150.148 NOTICE OF VIOLATION.
   The building inspector shall serve a notice of violation or order on the
person responsible for the construction, alteration, extension, repair,
removal, demolition, use or occupancy of a building or structure in violation
of any permit or certificate issued under the provisions of any code or
ordinance of the town; and such shall direct the discontinuance of the illegal
action or condition and abatement of the violation.
(Prior Code, § 4-604) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017)
§ 150.149 PROSECUTION OF VIOLATION.
   If the notice of violation or order is not complied with within the time set
forth therein, promptly, the building inspector shall request the Town Attorney
to institute the appropriate proceeding to restrain, correct or abate such
violation or to require the termination of the unlawful use of the building or
structure.
(Prior Code, § 4-605) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017)
§ 150.150 VIOLATION PENALTIES.
   Any person who shall violate a provision of any technical code adopted by
the town, the State Building Code or any ordinance of the town or shall fall to
comply with any of the requirements thereof or who shall erect, construct,
alter or repair a building or structure in violation of any certificate, notice
or order of the building inspector shall be fined.
(Prior Code, § 4-606) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017) Penalty, see §
150.999
§ 150.151 ABATEMENT OF VIOLATION.
   The imposition of the penalties herein prescribed shall not preclude the
Town Attorney from instituting appropriate action to prevent unlawful
construction or to restrain, correct or abate a violation, or to prevent
illegal occupancy of a building, structure or premises or to stop an illegal
act, conduct, business or use of a building or structure.
(Prior Code, § 4-607) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017)
§ 150.152 STOP WORK ORDER.
   Upon notice from the building inspector that work on any building or
structure is being prosecuted contrary to the provisions of any code or
ordinance of the town or in any unsafe or dangerous manner, such work shall be
immediately stopped. The building inspector is hereby authorized to issue a
stop work order, by a form promulgated by the building inspector for such
purpose. A stop work order shall be in writing and shall be posted on the
property in a conspicuous location; and shall state that all work must cease
forthwith and state the conditions under which work may be resumed. Such
posting shall constitute notice to the owner of such building or structure.
(Prior Code, § 4-608) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017)
§ 150.153 UNLAWFUL CONTINUANCE.
   Any person who shall continue any work in or about the building or structure
after posting of a stop work order, except such work as directed by the
building inspector to remove a violation or abate any unsafe condition, shall
be fined.
(Prior Code, § 4-609) (Ord. passed 8-28-2017) Penalty, see §
150.999
DANGEROUS OR UNHEALTHY STRUCTURES
§ 150.165 SCOPE.
   This subchapter is enacted pursuant to authority contained in W. Va. Code §
8-12-16, and nothing herein contained shall be construed to abrogate or impair
the power of any department of the town to enforce any provision of this code
or other ordinance or regulation, nor to prevent or punish violations; and the
powers conferred by this subchapter shall be in addition and supplemental to
the powers conferred by any other law of the state or ordinance of the town.
(Prior Code, § 4-701) (Ord. passed 8-3-2020)
§ 150.166 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this chapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   BUILDING CODES. The building codes adopted by the Town of Marlinton, West
Virginia pursuant to §§
150.015 and
150.016.
   BUILDING MAINTENANCE BOARD. The Building Maintenance Board of the Town of
Marlinton, West Virginia, as established and more particularly described in §§
33.15 through
33.19 of this code of ordinances.
   CIRCUIT COURT. The circuit court of Pocahontas County, West Virginia.
   MUNICIPALITY. The Town of Marlinton, West Virginia.
   OWNER or LANDOWNER. A person who individually or jointly with others:
      (1)   Has legal title to the property, with or without actual possession
of the property;
      (2)   Has charge, care or control of the property as owner or agent of
the owner;
      (3)   Is an executor, administrator, trustee or guardian of the estate of
the owner;
      (4)   Is the agent of the owner for the purpose of managing, controlling
or collecting rents; or
      (5)   May control or direct the management or disposition of the
property.
   UNSAFE BUILDING OR STRUCTURE. Any dwelling or other building unfit for human
habitation due to dilapidation, defects increasing and hazard of fire,
accidents or other calamities, lack of ventilation, light or sanitary
facilities or any other conditions prevailing in any dwelling or building,
whether used for human habitation or not, which would cause such building to be
unsafe, unsanitary, dangerous or detrimental to the public welfare.
   UNSAFE, UNSANITARY, DANGEROUS, OR DETRIMENTAL TO THE PUBLIC SAFETY OR
WELFARE.
      (1)   Any door, aisle, passageway, stairway, exit or other means of
egress that does not conform to the approved building or fire code of the
jurisdiction as related to the requirements for existing buildings;
      (2)   The walking surface of any aisle, passageway, stairway, exit or
other means of egress is so warped, worn loose, torn or otherwise unsafe as to
not provide safe and adequate means of egress;
      (3)   Any portion of a dwelling, building, structure or appurtenance that
has been damaged by fire, earthquake, wind, flood, deterioration, neglect,
abandonment, vandalism or by any other cause to an extent that it is likely to
partially or completely collapse, or to become detached or dislodged;
      (4)   Any portion of a structure or building, or any member, appurtenance
or ornamentation on the exterior that is not of sufficient strength or
stability, or is not so anchored, attached or fastened in place so as to be
capable of resisting natural or artificial loads of one and one-half the
original designed value;
      (5)   The dwelling, building or structure, or part of the building or
structure, because of dilapidation, deterioration, decay, faulty construction,
the removal or movement of some portion of the ground necessary for the
support, or for any other reason, is likely to partially or completely
collapse, or some portion of the foundation or underpinning of the dwelling,
building or structure is likely to fail or give way;
      (6)   The dwelling, building or structure, or any portion, is clearly
unsafe for its use;
      (7)   The dwelling, building or structure is neglected, damaged,
dilapidated, unsecured or abandoned so as to become an attractive nuisance to
children, becomes a harbor for vagrants, criminals and criminal activity, or
enables persons to resort to the dwelling, building or structure for committing
a nuisance or an unlawful act;
      (8)   Any dwelling, building, or structure constructed, exists or is
maintained in violation of any specific requirement or prohibition applicable
to any dwelling, building or structure provided by the approved building or
fire code of the jurisdiction or of any law or ordinance that presents either a
substantial risk of fire, building collapse or any other threat to life and
safety;
      (9)   A dwelling, building or structure, used or intended to be used for
dwelling purposes, because of inadequate maintenance, dilapidation, decay,
contamination by any hazardous substance or material, including, but not
limited to, substance resulting from the illegal manufacture of drugs, damage,
faulty construction or arrangement, inadequate light, ventilation, mechanical,
or plumbing system, or otherwise, is determined by the code enforcement agency
to be unsanitary, unfit for human habitation, or in a condition that is likely
to cause sickness or disease;
      (10)   Any dwelling, building or structure, because of a lack of
sufficient or proper fire resistance rated construction, fire protection
systems, electrical system, fuel connections, mechanical system, plumbing
system, or other cause, is determined by the code official to be a threat to
life or health; or
      (11)   Any portion of a building that remains on a site after the
demolition or destruction of the building or structure, or whenever any
building or structure is abandoned.
(Prior Code, § 4-702) (Ord. passed 8-3-2020)
§ 150.167 INSPECTIONS.
   (A)   The building inspector or his or her agent or agents shall inspect and
examine any dwelling or building within the town which, upon complaint of any
federal, state or municipal official or employee, or upon complaint of any
resident or citizen of the municipality, is alleged to constitute an unsafe
building or structure as herein defined; provided, that any entrance upon
premises for the purpose of making such inspection or examination shall be made
in such a manner as to cause the least possible inconvenience to the persons in
possession.
   (B)   Any inspections conducted pursuant to this chapter shall be consistent
with the following:
      (1)   Except in exigent circumstances and as permitted by law, the
building inspector shall provide reasonable advance notice to the owner and
request permission from the owner to enter the property;
      (2)   If the owner cannot be located after reasonable inquiry by the
building inspector as required by this section, or if the owner refuses entry,
the building inspector may obtain an administrative search warrant from either
the municipal court or the magistrate court located in the jurisdiction of the
municipality or county where the structure, dwelling or building is located.
Before obtaining an administrative search warrant, the building inspector is
required to make a sworn statement and prima facie case showing that the
building inspector was unable to gain access to the structure, dwelling or
building after reasonable and good faith efforts, and that there is a
legitimate and substantial safety concern involving the structure, dwelling, or
building that supports the requested entry;
      (3)   If granted by the court, and if the owner can be located, the
building inspector shall provide the owner a copy of the administrative search
warrant five days before entering the property. If applicable, the building
inspector shall also provide the same notice to any tenant or other person in
possession of the structure, dwelling or building; and
      (4)   Entry is for the sole purpose of inspection of the structure,
dwelling or building for unsafe or unsanitary conditions and not for the
purpose of criminal prosecution or gathering evidence for use in any criminal
charge or proceeding unrelated to the unsafe or unsanitary condition of the
structure, dwelling or building.
(Prior Code, § 4-703) (Ord. passed 8-3-2020)
§ 150.168 REPAIR, CLOSING, DEMOLITION OF UNSAFE STRUCTURES.
   (A)   When a building or structure or any portion thereof is, upon
inspection by the building inspector or his or her agent or agents, found to be
an unsafe building or structure as herein defined, the building inspector shall
issue a written complaint setting forth therein the name of the inspector, the
date of the inspection, the condition or conditions prevailing in such building
or structure which render it to be an unsafe building or structure as herein
defined and directing the repair, alteration, improvement or the vacating and
closing or removal or demolition, or any combination thereof, of such building
or structure, as the case may require, within a reasonable time to be set by
the building inspector. Such complaint shall further set a time and place for
hearing before the Building Maintenance Board at which time all interested
parties may appear and be heard.
   (B)   All complaints or orders issued by the building inspector shall be
served in accordance with the law of the state concerning the service of
process in civil actions, and shall, in addition thereto, be posted in a
conspicuous place on the premises affected by the complaint.
(Prior Code, § 4-704) (Ord. passed 8-3-2020)
§ 150.169 HEARINGS.
   If the directions of the building inspector as set forth in the complaint
are not carried out within the time specified therein, the Building Maintenance
Board shall conduct a hearing at the time and place set forth in the complaint
at which hearing all interested parties may appear, present evidence and be
heard with respect to such complaint.
(Prior Code, § 4-705) (Ord. passed 8-3-2020)
§ 150.170 ENFORCEMENT ORDERS; VIOLATIONS.
   (A)   If, after hearing the evidence presented at the hearing, the Building
Maintenance Board determines that the building or structure in question is an
unsafe building or structure as herein defined, the Building Maintenance Board
shall order that it be repaired, altered, improved, vacated, closed, removed or
demolished, or any combination thereof, as the case may require, within a time
to be set by the Building Maintenance Board and, if the owner or occupant of
such building or structure does not comply with such order within the time
specified, the town shall carry out the order and direction of the Building
Maintenance Board and shall assess all costs of such repairs, alterations,
improvements or such vacating and closing or removal or demolition, or any
combination thereof, to the owner of such building or structure, and such
costs, after the sale of any and all salvaged material is credited to the
account, shall be a lien against the real property upon which costs were
incurred.
   (B)   All orders issued by the Building Maintenance Board shall be served in
accordance with the law of the state concerning the service of process in civil
actions, and shall, in addition thereto, be posted in a conspicuous place on
the premises affected by the order.
   (C)   The Building Maintenance Board may enter orders providing for the
vacating, closing, removal or demolition of any dwelling, structure or
building, in the absence of owner agreement or court order provided that the
Building Maintenance Board provides lawful notice and undertakes reasonable
efforts to seek agreement from the owner before taking such action, and further
provided that:
      (1)   The dwelling, structure or building meets the definition of unsafe,
unsanitary, dangerous or detrimental to the public safety or welfare as set
forth in §
150.166, divisions (3), (4) or (8) of the definition for unsafe, unsanitary,
dangerous or detrimental to the public safety or welfare;
      (2)   The dwelling, structure, or building meets the definition of
unsafe, unsanitary, dangerous or detrimental to the public safety or welfare as
set forth in§
150.166, divisions (6), (7), (9) or (11) of the definition for unsafe,
unsanitary, dangerous or detrimental to the public safety or welfare, provided
that the dwelling, building or structure is vacant, abandoned or has been
lawfully declared unfit for human habitation; and the reasonable estimated cost
of repair, rehabilitation or corrective action exceeds the fair market value of
the dwelling, building or structure;
      (3)   If the Building Maintenance Board cannot effect personal service on
the owner, a Building Maintenance Board official shall subscribe a written
affidavit, to be maintained for a minimum of two years, that demonstrates the
structure, dwelling or building falls within one of the categories set forth
division (C)(1) or (C)(2) above, and sets forth the basis in reasonable detail,
including documentation of same, and memorializes the Building Maintenance
Board’s efforts to contact or get permission for entry and any corrective
action from the owner; and the Building Maintenance Board shall publish notice
of its intent to enter the property for the purpose of demolition or
correction, along with the address of the property, the name of the owners and
the date of the proposed action, as a Class II legal advertisement consistent
with the requirements of W. Va. Code § 59-3-2, the first of which shall run at
least 30 days before the date of the proposed action by the enforcement agency,
and the last being no later than 20 days before the date of the proposed action
by the enforcement agency; and
      (4)   If there is no response to the notice by the owner or landowner in
the time specified in the notice, then the town may proceed in correction or
demolition of the subject dwelling, building or structure.
   (D)   It is an absolute defense to any civil action by an owner, landowner
or tenant for damages resulting from the closure, demolition or other
corrective action taken by the town under this section; provided, that the town
acted in good faith, can demonstrate that the structure, dwelling or building
falls within one of the categories set forth in division (C)(1) or (C)(2)
above, that the town followed the procedures set forth in this division (D),
and that the town had adopted the State Building Code at the time of the
closure, demolition or other corrective action occurred.
   (E)   Any owner or occupant of any building or structure affected by any
complaint or order of the Building Maintenance Board, as well as the town,
shall have the right to apply to the circuit court for a temporary injunction
restraining the enforcement of any order of the Building Maintenance Board
pending final disposition of the cause, as provided in W. Va. Code § 8-12-16.
   (F)   It shall be unlawful for any owner, occupant, lessee or other person
in interest of such dwelling, building or structure as determined by the
Building Maintenance Board to be dangerous, unhealthy or unfit for human
habitation, to fail to comply with any order to repair, vacate or demolish and
remove same, or any other order of the Building Maintenance Board from which no
appeal or other remedy has been invoked. The imposition of one penalty for any
violation shall not excuse subsequent violations or deny subsequent
impositions, fines or imprisonment or both for continuing violations; and all
such persons shall be required to correct or remedy such violations or defects
within a reasonable time, and when not otherwise specified, each ten days that
prohibited conditions continue, shall constitute a separate offense.
   (G)   It shall be unlawful for any person to remove any notice or order of
the building inspector and/or Building Maintenance Board posted as required
under any of the provisions of the chapter.
(Prior Code, § 4-706) (Ord. passed 8-3-2020) Penalty, see §
150.999

   (B)   There is hereby adopted the International Plumbing Code, 2015 Edition
and one copy of which shall remain on file in the office of the Mayor and such
Code is hereby incorporated in and made a part of this chapter as fully as if

until the applicable fee required by the particular permit applied for shall be

applied for has been paid. The Town Council shall establish a schedule of fees
for permits and inspections required by the town’s Electrical Code.
